## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force contains nonlinear terms in position (e.g., Duffing-type) and potentially explicit time-dependent driving or parametric terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (linear oscillator with sinusoidal driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (cubic nonlinearity with driving)
- Damped driven oscillator (implicit): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * x**2 (asymmetric nonlinearity with driving)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric Duffing)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order Duffing)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (parametric excitation)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametric resonance)
- Van der Pol type (position proxy): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * sin(c3 * t)
- Driven with damping proxy: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t)
- Softening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * sin(c3 * t)
- Nonlinear with combined time terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * t * sin(c3 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium; even powers (x²) break symmetry
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms additive to the restoring force
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between x and trigonometric functions of t
- Hardening springs have same-sign cubic terms as linear term (c0*x + c1*x³ with c0*c1 > 0 in restoring sense); softening springs have opposite sign
- If acceleration depends on t only through periodic functions, the system is periodically driven or parametrically excited
- Absence of explicit velocity variable suggests damping may be negligible or the task focuses on conservative + driving forces
- Multiple frequency components in driving suggest superposition of sinusoidal terms: c0*sin(c1*t) + c2*sin(c3*t)
- Position-dependent frequency modulation appears as x*cos(c*t) cross-terms indicating parametric coupling

- `-1.99164100804766*x*(0.0248350833882069*t + 1)` = `-0.0494770846498*x*t - 1.99164100804766*x` → x·t term and x term

The candidates use terms like `x*cos(c*t)`, `x*sin(c*t)`, `cos(c*t+c)`, `sin(c*t+c)`, etc. None of these can produce a term linear in t (like `x*t`), because:
- `cos(c*t)` with any constant c gives a periodic function, not a linear function of t
- `sin(c*t)` similarly
- Setting frequency to 0 gives a constant, not a linear function

The only way to get `x*t` would be through some non-periodic function of t. Let me check for any candidates with unusual terms:

- Candidate 38: has `sin(c7 + c8*t + c9*x)` - this is still periodic in t
- Candidate 35: has `t*sin(c8*t + c9)` - this has t multiplied by sin, but not x*t

None of the candidates can produce a pure `x*t` term. All t-dependent terms in the candidates are trigonometric (periodic), while the GT requires a term that grows linearly with t.
